    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

  <span id="freeText18084843203596155428" style="display:none"><i>There was once a time when darkness shrouded the world, and the darkness had a queen.</i><br /><br />Adelina Amouteru is done suffering. She’s turned her back on those who have betrayed her and achieved the ultimate revenge: victory. Her reign as the White Wolf has been a triumphant one, but with each conquest her cruelty only grows. The darkness within her has begun to spiral out of control, threatening to destroy all she’s gained.<br /><br />When a new danger appears, Adelina’s forced to revisit old wounds, putting not only herself at risk, but every Elite. In order to preserve her empire, Adelina and her Roses must join the Daggers on a perilous quest—though this uneasy alliance may prove to be the real danger.</span>

<div id="review_1388684337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1388684337" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1388684337?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1388684337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12743613353590699857"><blockquote>
  <i>“Not invincible after all, little wolf?"</i>
</blockquote><br/>I only wish this book was longer. After all the violence, emotions and drama of this series, this final installment was a good hundred pages too short for me (and it's not often I say that). True, it pretty much ended the way I expected, the only way it really could, but the journey there has been <b>bloody, twisted, and a whole lot of fun</b>.<br/><br/>The end of the last book threw a dark little twist at us and I couldn't wait to find out more about Adelina's state o</span>
  <span id="freeText12743613353590699857" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Not invincible after all, little wolf?"</i>
</blockquote><br />I only wish this book was longer. After all the violence, emotions and drama of this series, this final installment was a good hundred pages too short for me (and it's not often I say that). True, it pretty much ended the way I expected, the only way it really could, but the journey there has been <b>bloody, twisted, and a whole lot of fun</b>.<br /><br />The end of the last book threw a dark little twist at us and I couldn't wait to find out more about Adelina's state of mind in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28588345.The_Midnight_Star__The_Young_Elites___3_" title="The Midnight Star (The Young Elites, #3) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Star</a>. Would she redeem herself? Would she continue spiralling into darkness, becoming ever more consumed by her desire for power? As this book opens, we see just how far gone she is. Now a powerful queen, she rules with fear and pain.<br /><br />Adelina, herself, makes this story so gripping. <b>She is the perfect antihero</b>. Despicable, and yet so easy to sympathize with. Lu ties us to her pain and suffering, so that we want her to succeed and find happiness even as she causes so much destruction. In fact, it is the twisted, somewhat evil characters that drive this series. Even the repulsive Teren fascinates. Here, we see more of his story, which develops a complex layer to his loathsome character. I always kind of loved to hate him, and here I also kind of just loved him. A little bit. Shh, don't judge me.<br /><br />Parts of this book are creepy; other parts are sad, but without being overly-sentimental. The death toll creeps up and all lives lost hit me hard. Lu has gotten better at crafting those <b>perfectly subtle scenes</b> that tug at my heart strings far more than any melodramatic heartbreak ever could. It's quietly sad. And somehow that hurts most of all.<br /><br />I thought the conclusion was inevitable, though it was no less perfect because of its predictability. No less effective. Afterwards, Lu closes the story with a small folk tale from the future: the immortal story of the White Wolf, who may have been a courageous hero or a cruel villain. Depending which version of the story you've heard.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>

<div id="review_1130709618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130709618" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1130709618?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well">he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=great-but-not-quite-there-yet">great-but-not-quite-there-yet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=when-sparks-don-t-fly">when-sparks-don-t-fly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=lgbtqia-if-you-squint">lgbtqia-if-you-squint</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bittersweet-ending">bittersweet-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=insta-love-add-water">insta-love-add-water</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1130709618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18048791966448521528"><blockquote>
  <i>"Sometimes I can't tell if my madness is what's conjuring these images, twisting my confidence. So I try to ignore them, as always. What does it matter if I'm mad? I have a hundred ships. Twenty thousand soldiers. My Roses at my side. I am queen."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478522803ra/21081047.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I think <b>the series peaked at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23846013.The_Rose_Society__The_Young_Elites___2_' title='The Rose Society (The Young Elites, #2) by Marie Lu' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rose Society</a>.</b> After that spine-chilling ending and months of waiting for The Midnight Star to show (I actually had to wait three weeks more because Book Depository fucked up), the end product seems <b>rather underwhelmi</b></span>
  <span id="freeText18048791966448521528" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Sometimes I can't tell if my madness is what's conjuring these images, twisting my confidence. So I try to ignore them, as always. What does it matter if I'm mad? I have a hundred ships. Twenty thousand soldiers. My Roses at my side. I am queen."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478522803ra/21081047.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think <b>the series peaked at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23846013.The_Rose_Society__The_Young_Elites___2_" title="The Rose Society (The Young Elites, #2) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose Society</a>.</b> After that spine-chilling ending and months of waiting for The Midnight Star to show (I actually had to wait three weeks more because Book Depository fucked up), the end product seems <b>rather underwhelming.</b> I closed the book thinking, "Is that it?"and didn't spend any more time time pondering over the characters and themes. When I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14290364.Champion__Legend___3_" title="Champion (Legend, #3) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Champion</a> on the other hand, I was inconsolable for the rest of the night.<br><br>I sort of <b>anticipated the ending,</b> but I didn't expect it go down the way it did. It ruins the dark, morally grey aspect the marketing team keeps selling The Young Elites as. Adelina is evil! She's an anti-heroine! In reality, she's a young girl who lost her way, but always belonged to the light. She's not a villain-in-making; she's a villain looking for redemption. Marie Lu made her a <b>little too sympathetic.</b> Maybe my personal definition of antihero is to blame, but when I think morally questionable, I think Kaz Brekker from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156.Six_of_Crows__Six_of_Crows___1_" title="Six of Crows (Six of Crows, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a>. I think Tyrion Lannister or Daenerys Targaryen. The best villains don't seek to redeem themselves because they don't see anything to redeem.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478523361ra/21081146.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Am I a horrible person for wanting Adelina to stay dead? It would have added to the legend of the White Wolf. Was she a good ruler? A bad one? Depends on which story you hear.<br><br>And it's not fair leaving Magiano in this limbo state. She can only return at night, right? What's he supposed to do for the rest of his life? Keep following her through the night, wanting but never fully having? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The Midnight Star is <b>pretty short</b> in terms of finales, too. Only 311 pages. That's usually a bad sign because it means there's not a lot of story to tell, and what little there is will be stretched out like pasta. But here, there's a <b>lot of story that's left out.<br><br>Magiano could have been developed more.</b> His backstory, ambitions, and everything that makes a character are barely touched upon. He went from being a clever, loyal thief with his own agenda in The Rose Society to Generic Love Interest #101. The kind that will take a bullet for the protagonist without the much needed development for justification. I suppose he grew closer to Adelina in the year's time between the events of The Rose Society and The Midnight Star, but it ain't canon unless it's on the page. <br><br>Raffaele and Enzo, and Lucent and Maeve are other examples. You can't just throw these LGBT couples at us, say, "I did representation!" and not develop them into well-crafted pairings with their own pulse and heartbeat. To be fair, Violetta and Sergio don't get much fleshing out either, so it's a matter of time, not skill. But dammit, if <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156.Six_of_Crows__Six_of_Crows___1_" title="Six of Crows (Six of Crows, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a> can develop three realistic, individual fandom-worthy pairings in two books, then The Young Elites can do it in three.<br><br>The magic/religion elements were just weird. I don't even want to talk about it. Feel free to engage me in the comments though.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478523206ra/21081126.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Adelina and Violetta's relationship was one of the few bright spots.</b> Even though they're apart for a large part of the narrative, their sisterly bond continues to flourish and grow. The climax is all about them. Not Magiano, not Enzo, not Sergio. Just two sisters. That scene near the end was magnificent and why I ultimately rated this four stars. I like books that tear my heart in two.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"'Sisters forever,' Violetta declared, in her tiny, young voice.<br><br>Until death, even in death, even beyond." </i>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/812274972" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Young Elites</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130709603" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Rose Society</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1085984226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1085984226" />
    <a title="Fari " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30492707-fari"><img alt="Fari " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473185113p2/30492707.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1085984226?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fari " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fari " href="/user/show/30492707-fari">Fari </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30492707-fari?shelf=opinion-didn-t-see-that-coming">opinion-didn-t-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30492707-fari?shelf=genre-young-adult">genre-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30492707-fari?shelf=genre-weird-and-creepy">genre-weird-and-creepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30492707-fari?shelf=opinion-bittersweet">opinion-bittersweet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30492707-fari?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30492707-fari?shelf=series-finished">series-finished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30492707-fari?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30492707-fari?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30492707-fari?shelf=book-3">book-3</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30492707-fari?shelf=opinion-worthy-of-tears">opinion-worthy-of-tears</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085984226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9282162390657080883"><p>
  <i>You cannot harden your heart to the future just because of your past. You cannot use cruelty against yourself to justify cruelty to others.</i>
</p><p><br/>Good News & Bad News: Marie Lu knows how to end her trilogies with a bang but also knows how to kill her readers. I feel as though I am not even alive anymore. I am writing this review after my death, my funeral was yesterday and I’m surprised how good the Wi-Fi is, considering I’m in a coffin. (Okay, this scenario is running away from me, let’s stop.)<br/><br/>Mar</p></span>
  <span id="freeText9282162390657080883" style="display:none"><p>
  <i>You cannot harden your heart to the future just because of your past. You cannot use cruelty against yourself to justify cruelty to others.</i>
</p><p><br />Good News &amp; Bad News: Marie Lu knows how to end her trilogies with a bang but also knows how to kill her readers. I feel as though I am not even alive anymore. I am writing this review after my death, my funeral was yesterday and I’m surprised how good the Wi-Fi is, considering I’m in a coffin. (Okay, this scenario is running away from me, let’s stop.)<br /><br />Marie Lu’s endings, both Champion and The Midnight Star, have been very bittersweet. I'm usually hesitant to read endings of series and trilogies because it can all go horribly wrong and ruin the series. However, I now know I really don't have to worry about that with Marie Lu's endings. They do not leave things hanging and give readers the proper closure they deserve but oh my gosh, do they destroy the reader’s heart anyway. In my opinion, Midnight Star was even better than Champion, so if you’ve read that and are about to read MS, strap yourselves in! It felt as though my heart had been broken a million and 1 times but has only been healed a million. <br /></p><p>
  <i>I am the nightmare.</i>
</p><p><br />This book starts epically. It is intense and dark and gruesome and makes you heart beat out of your chest. It was shorter than Rose Society and much more fast-paced, which I appreciated. I am not joking when I say that I missed my station and rode the TTC for two more stops before realising that I had been so caught up in an intense scene that I had forgotten about the real world. I am ashamed (because how Fari? why?) but I also applaud Marie Lu (because how Marie? Why?). <br /></p><p>
  <i>None of us are saints. We can all do better.</i>
</p><p><br />This book I think was very plot driven with certain characters’ arcs. I do wish we got some more quality character development and interactions, though. The cast of characters in this trilogy is pretty big and I don’t think Marie Lu used that aspect to its full potential. <br /><br />While we got to know some characters extremely well and they had character arcs to cry and die for, some characters I still barely know the names of, even after 3 books. Some characters I know in depth and some characters I forget exist until Marie Lu mentions them (which might be about once every 50 pages). I’m not talking about minor, minor characters, btw. I’m talking about side characters being treated as minor, minor characters. There are characters from Young Elites group, like Michael, and Sergio from Adelina’s own Rose Society, who I barely know even though they are there in various/most scenes. I just wish that wasn’t the case. I think some important characters were created to serve only one purpose and after that was done, they were there on the sidelines but were rarely mentioned or developed as characters. <br /></p><p>
  <i>After a lifetime of darkness, I want to leave something behind that is made of light.</i>
</p><p><br />I definitely don’t hate that romance in this book, or even the trilogy, but I didn’t really care for until the very end of this book. Which was slightly strange because I loved both Adelina and both of the guys she showed interest in. (Not that there is a love triangle in this book, just in general in the trilogy) I also wanted more of the queen and Lucent’s love and how they had to fight for it because that was extremely interesting. We got very little of that, which was disappointing; I wanted Marie Lu to explore their relationship just a little bit more. It was only mentioned about two to three times in the book, though. <br /></p><p>
  <i>We are doomed to be forever young.</i>
</p><p><br />This book definitely is a step up from Rose Society and receives a glowing 4/5 stars. It was action-packed and feels-inducing but certain aspects I wanted explored were not explored.<br />If you liked Legend, READ THIS TRILOGY. If you were meh about Legend, still give this trilogy a chance.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="9282162390657080883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2639644397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2639644397" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2639644397?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2639644397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4535527229191884153"><b>
  <i>‘to those who, in spite of everything, still choose goodness.’</i>
</b><br/><br/>ughhh. im not crying, you are… even from the opening dedication, i knew this book was going to be something else. <br/><br/>and i will admit, i really had to think about how i felt after i finished the last page of this final instalment. because this was not the conclusion i was hoping for, or even expecting. but after some reflection, i realised maybe it was the resolution that was needed. and heres why.<br/><br/>even though the storyline doesnt rea</span>
  <span id="freeText4535527229191884153" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‘to those who, in spite of everything, still choose goodness.’</i>
</b><br /><br />ughhh. im not crying, you are… even from the opening dedication, i knew this book was going to be something else. <br /><br />and i will admit, i really had to think about how i felt after i finished the last page of this final instalment. because this was not the conclusion i was hoping for, or even expecting. but after some reflection, i realised maybe it was the resolution that was needed. and heres why.<br /><br />even though the storyline doesnt really feel connected to the first two books, even though the world building ive been waiting ages for feels like an out-of-place dump of random information, and even though <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the death of enzo (and many other characters) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was completely glanced over and not properly acknowledged as it should have been, i realised the point of this series is not about any of that. it isnt about the plot direction or the world building. these books are about one thing, and one thing only. <br /><br />and that is the development of adelina. <br /><br />those who have read this series will know what i mean. to explain the depth of the changes she goes through would make this review so much longer than it needs to be. in this book, she makes the comment, <i>‘after a lifetime of darkness, i want to leave something behind that is made of light.’</i> and i swear, when i read the final epilogue and understood the touching significance of the title, i could feel my heart just swell in size. i may not have liked adelina very much as a character, but i cannot deny that she has had one of the most outstanding character arcs i have ever read. and so to me, looking at this book in terms of how i feel about the conclusion in regard to adelinas story, well, then that is what makes it worth something. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1433829607" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1433829607" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1433829607?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1433829607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6020563572638937082"><b>3.75</b>, but I'm rounding it down to three all the same because Marie Lu can do so much better, and this book left such a bad taste in my mouth, I'll need a Nutella-based diet for the rest of my life.<br/><br/><b>"These are only rumors, of course, and make little more than a story to tell around the fire. But it is <i>told</i>. And thus they live on."</b><br/><br/>•The first book in this series, <i>The Young Elites</i> is among my all-time favourite books. This simple fact, I think, tells enough about how much I cared and how many hopes I</span>
  <span id="freeText6020563572638937082" style="display:none"><b>3.75</b>, but I'm rounding it down to three all the same because Marie Lu can do so much better, and this book left such a bad taste in my mouth, I'll need a Nutella-based diet for the rest of my life.<br /><br /><b>"These are only rumors, of course, and make little more than a story to tell around the fire. But it is <i>told</i>. And thus they live on."</b><br /><br />•The first book in this series, <i>The Young Elites</i> is among my all-time favourite books. This simple fact, I think, tells enough about how much I cared and how many hopes I had for this conlcusion. This obviously compels me to wonder, were said hopes too high? Was I too enthusiastic? Was it <i>my</i> fault, or the book's? Because, my fellow readers, <i>The Midnight Star</i> felt very- no, <b>way too underwhelming</b>.<br /> If you rapidly scroll down this page, you will find that, when the title was revealed, my reaction was one of excitement, yes, but mixed with some perplexity about its utter diversity from the other two in the series. As I said in that occasion, it is my impression that it has literally <i>nothing</i> to do with those. It doesn't even seem to belong to the same series. Well, now I can say that <b>the title was indeed symptomatic</b>, as <i>The Midnight Star</i>, under many points of views, has little in common with both <i>The Young Elites</i> and the <i>The Rose Society</i>. <b>The continuity was disrupted</b>. The causes/reasons are manifold.<br /><br />•I've already pointed out that Marie Lu, in this book, appears to be rather <b>below par</b>. In this final installment, <b>there's none of the liveliness of writing and characterization she let us get used to: the characters are dull, the storytelling is dull, the plot is dull</b>. The only things worth mentioning that actually take place and <i>happen</i> are all condensed in the last page, and they don't even feel squeezed - but probably we should have gleaned that, for the author, very little was left to said. From where? The number of pages, basically a handful of them, which did make me suspicious at first. And indeed, <b>the shortness of the book does not help</b> in softening my judgement - if anything,<b> it adds to my confusion</b>.<br /><br />•The dynamics between the characters used to be subtle and yet soulful- absolutely spectacular. Where did <i>that</i> go? All of them do <i>exactly</i> what you already expect them to do, say exactly what you already expect them to say. <b>Boring</b>. <b>Nothing at all is added to their characterizations</b>, with no exception. Magiano and Adelina, for one thing: I did not think it as possible to feel such a black, sad <i>nothing</i> for a couple I used to ship so hard. And further on, where is Adelina's depth? Where is her struggle? And I do not need to be showed illusions and nightmares. <i>Show me her heart</i>, because I cannot see it anymore. <br />For heaven's sake, <i>
  <b>where is the <i>pathos</i>?</b>
</i><br /><br />•<b>The deaths</b>, not necessarily in chronological order.<br />1) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>Enzo</b>'d (definitive) death: horrifyingly anticlimactic. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And throughout the previous chapters, this character (I'm not even revealing the gender; see how good I am?) had barely uttered a word. If that's the right way to handle a character, I should probably stop studying literature because clearly my efforts have been devastatingly fruitless up to now. <br />2) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>Teren</b>'s death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>: it seems almost wrong to even comment on this one because this character basically had no role in this book. It was there, but nothing would have changed if it weren't. <br />3) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>Violetta</b>'s just-joking-death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>: so let me understand, I really am supposed to think it didn't happen only in order to provide an excuse so <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Adelina's kind-of-death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> could happen?<br />4) And finally, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Adelina's death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I must admit <b>I am rather conflicted about this one</b>. I won't try to say it wasn't beautiful in its own way, but I can't help wondering, was it necessary? Or better, was it necessary <i>like this</i>, in this circumstance? What I mean is, it was pretty obvious it was going to happen. I was prepared, I was even favourable to it - I knew it was one of the ways, the most powerful one at that, in which this ending could really become meaningful. But the way it happened- it was just <b>trivial</b> and <b>trite</b>, <b>run-of-the-mill</b>. It was supposed to be such a strong and significant act, and its <i>supposed-ness</i> was exactly what made it devoid of significance. Like, you tried so hard, but in the end it didn't matter. <br /><br />•(Part of the following criticism, I acknowledge it, is due to my very personal taste, so feel free to not consider it if you're trying to decide whether to read the book and you feel you don't mind about this specific detail.)<br />The thing is: why do the gods <i>obviously</i> have to win? Not counting the fact that <b>the divine element</b> was trotted out a bit arbitrarily, in my opinion, just kind of like when all the cutest guys already have a date for prom (and would never have so much as looked at you in the first place) and you've got to settle for the one mediocre offer you get. Anyway, the point is that the gods win, men submit. I do not agree that that should be a given, also because (and here restarts the wannabe-objective critique), is it really believable that not one of the most powerful Elites in the known world even just <i>tries</i> to think of a way around it? In a rush to get to the (rushed) conclusion, everyone, the author for one, forgot what "alternative" means. <b>Too simplistic</b>, <b>too clumsy</b>, <b>too hurried</b>. And, for my taste, too preconceived too.<br /><br />•What I utterly adored was the idea of the story that lived on. That's a <i>motif</i> I've always loved. It was physiological.<br /><br />➽ Until I put down all the things that had bothered me, I hadn't realized <i>The Midnight Star</i> had left me so disappointed. <b>The Elites series still is and will remain one of my absolute favorites</b>, but I don't think I could ever get back to thinking of it in the terms of sheer perfection I associated it to before. This ending was handled far too sloppily for me to turn a blind eye, and I won't recover from this quickly; but I'll sill kill everyone who dares deny<b> Adelina Amouteru is one of the greatest and best-written characters of young-adult literature</b>. <br /><br /><br /><b>PRE-READING</b><br /><b>EDIT</b> 30/07/16: <b>First chapter</b> here!<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bustle.com/articles/171783-the-midnight-star-concludes-marie-lus-dark-twisted-young-elites-series-exclusive-excerpt">http://www.bustle.com/articles/171783...</a><br />I am afraid to read and I'm dying for it at same time. How is that possible?<br /><br /><b>EDIT</b> 25/01/16: I feel like this title has absolutely nothing to do with the other two but I like it all the same.<br /><br /><b>EDIT</b> 14/11/15: This one scares me so much it's actually giving me nightmares. I swear it is. Marie Lu has stolen my nighttime. Now tell me, how on earth is that possible?<br />Man, this woman.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6020563572638937082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2598105067" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2598105067?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141361840" href="/book/show/30112193-the-midnight-star">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2598105067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7242219901673162495"><i>”The day will come when we strike you down,” she’s saying. “Mark my words. We will haunt your nightmares.” <br/>I clench my fists and fling an illusion of pain across her body. “I am the nightmare.”</i><br/><br/>Ohh this was so nice to read! Do you remember how much I liked the <b>“Rose Society”</b> because all the characters were so morally grey and no one was entirely bad or good? Well, this final book was even more intriguing and I loved that I couldn’t decide whether I liked them or hated them. XD The funny thing is </span>
  <span id="freeText7242219901673162495" style="display:none"><i>”The day will come when we strike you down,” she’s saying. “Mark my words. We will haunt your nightmares.” <br />I clench my fists and fling an illusion of pain across her body. “I am the nightmare.”</i><br /><br />Ohh this was so nice to read! Do you remember how much I liked the <b>“Rose Society”</b> because all the characters were so morally grey and no one was entirely bad or good? Well, this final book was even more intriguing and I loved that I couldn’t decide whether I liked them or hated them. XD The funny thing is that some of those characters, mostly Teren and Adelina, are ruthless and cruel while they pursue their goals, yet they are still insecure and wounded by their past. Sure, they maintain a tough and unemotional exterior but deep down within them they are as vulnerable as everyone else! <br /><br />I think it’s exactly that inner conflict which appeals to me so much! Marie Lu made it impossible to choose a side because if it comes down to it there is no noble or right side to choose. Neither of them is perfect, they all follow their own path and act according to their own set of rules. Admittedly some of them with more compassion than others, but in the end they all do their own thing, weighting advantage against disadvantage, using their people and resources as a means to an end. <br /><br />This of course led to a lot of distrust and tension between the diverse cast of characters and I wouldn’t be me if I wouldn’t have enjoyed their animosity and distrust with gusto! ;-P I literally live and breathe for situations like that so I was a very happy camper indeed, basking in their potential for conflict. (must be the cunning faerie in me! *lol*) Anyway, let’s not dwell on the faerie that’s inside of me but go to the fun part of my review instead! ;-)<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><u>Welcome to my “Spoilery spoiler section”! If you don’t want to know what happens in the book I suggest you don’t read any further, because if you do, you’ll be spoiled without mercy. *lol* If you still decide to read on: Don’t say I didn’t warn you! It’s at your own risk! ;-P</u><br /><br /><b>Adelina:</b><br /><br /><i>”What does it matter if I’m mad? I have a hundred ships. Twenty thousand soldiers. My Roses at my side. I am queen.”</i><br /><br />And here I thought that Adelina was already dark in <b>“The Rose Society”</b>. Well, seems like I’ve been wrong. There is always a possibility to step up your game. ;-) At the beginning of this book Adelina isn’t only the Queen of Kenettra but also conquered the Sealands and thus has become the Queen of the Sealands as well. She’s ruthless, harsh and has absolutely no compassion for the people that hurt her so much. In fact she’s become exactly what Teren and the Inquisition were for her and the worst part: She even enjoys it. Talk about monsters that are created! &gt;_&lt; Still, there’s some humanity left in her and every once in a while Magiano manages to coax it out of her. It’s not enough to genuinely like her, but it also makes it very difficult to dislike her for her actions. *lol* Damn! Marie Lu, you wrote her well! XD<br /><br /><b>Raffaele:</b><br /><br /><i>”We were never meant to exist, Adelina,” he says. “And we will never exist again. But we cannot take the entire world with us.” He meets my gaze. “No matter how it has wronged us.”</i><br /><br />Ohh, my Raffaele!!! I still love this boy to bits and pieces and this time around we were even able to see a great deal of his inner strength. Enzo’s pain and suffering hurt him so much, yet he still tried to be there for him and did his best to keep him away from the abyss of the underworld. In the end the goddess of death claimed his love though and jeez, how much I suffered with him when Enzo died!!! Despite everything that happened he wasn’t filled with bitterness though. He still tried to do the right thing and took care not only of his daggers but also of the rest of the world. Hell, he was so brave facing the goddess of death! I can’t even!!! <b>I JUST LOVE MY BOY!!! &lt;333</b><br /><br /><i>”We are here to save those like ourselves,” Raffaele answers. He must be afraid of her, as are we all, but his voice stays steady and gentle, unrelenting. “We are here to save the mortal world.”</i><br /><br /><b>Teren:</b><br /><br /><i>”Trusting me,” Teren murmurs, “is a dangerous game, mi Adelinetta.”</i> <br /><br />I know this might sound strange but I actually felt sorry for Teren! XD Even though he didn’t show it and hid it behind his typical acid comments it was still obvious that the death of Guilietta broke him. He was just a shell of his former self and it truly hurt me to see him like that. There wasn’t much he believed in but he loved Guilietta and he despised malfettos like himself. Within a few moments Adelina managed to turn his entire world upside down and I can’t even imagine the self-hatred he had to deal with while he was imprisoned in his cell. In the end he did the right thing though and I think he might actually be happy now. Well, at least I hope he is. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><b>Violetta:</b><br /><br /><i>”You cannot harden your heart to the future just because of your past. You cannot use cruelty against yourself to justify cruelty to others.”</i> <br /><br />Well, Violetta’s development was certainly unexpected. I mean I expected her to seek out the daggers after what Adelina did to her at the end of “The Rose Society” but I definitely didn’t expect her to get ill so fast. It was so sad when she died and the moment Adelina realized it broke my heart. T_T After everything that happened I’m glad that Adelina decided to trade her life for hers though. I’m sure Violetta is a good queen and with Raffaele at her side they might as well have many years of peace and prosperity. =))<br /><br /><b>Magiano:</b><br /><br /><i>”As he sailed away into the dawn, he made himself two promises.<br />One: He would always have a name, and that name would be Magiano.<br />And two: No matter what happened, he would carry joy with him. Almost as if he were carrying her.”</i><br /><br />Interestingly enough, Magiano seemed to be the only one who didn’t suffer all too much from the use of his abilities. Was it because he could only mimic the powers of others and therefore didn’t have a specific kind of ability that would have hastened his deterioration? I don’t know, but whatever it was I’m grateful for it. Aside from Violetta he was the only person Adelina listened to and I don’t even want to know what she would have done without his steady presence at her side. Maybe burned everything without a second glance. *lol* Well, anyway! It was really nice to finally get a little bit of his backstory and I soaked it up like a greedy sponge. Poor Magiano though! He would have deserved so much better than what he got in the end. =(((<br /><br /><b>The relationships:</b><br /><br /><u>Adelina &amp; Magiano:</u><br /><br /><i>”You paint me as a saint,” he murmurs. “But I aligned with greed solely to prevent that.”</i><br /><br />I loved this ship and all their interactions! &lt;333 They could have been so great together if only Adelina’s whispers wouldn’t have controlled her actions so much! *sighs* I really wish they would have had a chance to be happy together but Marie Lu obviously had another story in mind. &gt;_&lt; Gosh, it broke my heart that Adelina is the Midnight Star now and that Magiano couldn’t spend his entire life with her. Still, the legend at the end of the book gave me hope and I want to believe that those meetings actually happened and that they found their way back to each other in the end! T_T So sad and tragic and bittersweet! *sniff* <br /><br /><u>Adelina &amp; Teren:</u><br /><br /><i>”You don’t deserve to wear her face,” he whispers.<br />I smile bitterly. “Let’s not forget who killed her. You destroy all that you touch.”<br />“Well,” he whispers back, returning my smile. “Then we have much in common.”</i> <br /><br />Ha! There is no love lost between those two but I think they eventually managed to make their peace. I mean at the end of the book Adelina hopes that Teren will be happy in the underworld and Teren helped her to survive long enough to restore the balance of their world so I guess they both got what they wanted even though it had a slightly different outcome than they imagined…<br /><br /><u>Raffaele &amp; Enzo:</u><br /><br /><i>”He can sense the agony hovering over the prince, and the feeling scalds his own heart as surely as if he were wounded himself.”</i><br /><br />Okay, it’s official! Marie Lu didn’t hear my prayers and decided to crush my ship! T_T <b>WHY??!!!</b> It makes me so sad that their relationship had no chance to bloom and I’m deeply wounded by the fact that my precious Raffaele didn’t even get a single kiss or at least an “I love you.” from the lips of the love of his life! *sniff* I’m so sad; I’m going to hide in a corner and lick my wounds now. T_T<br /><br /><u>Violetta &amp; Adelina:</u><br /><br /><i>”After a lifetime of darkness, I want to leave something behind that is made of light.” Both of her hands cup my face. Violetta stares at me with a look of determination, and then she brings me to her and hugs me close. “You are a light,” she replies gently. “And when you shine, you shine bright.”</i><br /><br />I loved the relationship between those two! &lt;333 They had their arguments and troubles but through it all that they were still two sisters that cared about each other deeply!!! Plus Violetta truly was Adelina’s conscience! I’m so proud of Adelina for choosing to give her life for Violetta, to give it to her willingly because she loves her sister and wants her to live the life she never had! She could have decided to go back herself but she wanted Violetta to live! That is love!!! &lt;333 That is compassion, a sacrifice and altruism and <b>GAH!!!</b> I’m so proud of Adelina!!! But also sad… so sad that it had to end like that. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br />Despite my broken heart I still think that this last book was a good conclusion to the entire series. Marie Lu didn’t give me the happily ever after I wished for but she definitely managed to keep my attention and after all the turmoils the characters had to go through she even ended it on a positive and hopeful note. I’m not happy but I’m satisfied and that has to count for something, right?! *lol*<br /><br />______________________________<br /><br /><u>
  <b>PREVIEW:</b>
</u><br /><br />So I’ve already reached the last book of this amazing series and it feels like I read this in a year! (Which I probably did, because I think I finished the first book at the beginning of this year?! *lol*) <br /><br />Either way, I’m really looking forward to read <b>“The Midnight Star”</b>. I want to know what happens to those two different groups, especially after the ending of <b>“The Rose Society”</b>. <br />Plus you all know why I actually read this series. <br /><br />The reason is one name and one name alone: <br /><b>
  <u>Raffaele Laurent Bessette</u>
</b><br /><br />I love him so damn much! &lt;333 <br />This said, let’s jump right into the fun! ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7242219901673162495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1711054661" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1711054661" />
    <a title="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10376232-saania-zee-jamal"><img alt="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495529362p2/10376232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1711054661?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Saania Zee Jamal ϟ" href="/user/show/10376232-saania-zee-jamal">Saania Zee Jamal ϟ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=dear-lord-have-mercy-on-me">dear-lord-have-mercy-on-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=yawn">yawn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=remind-me-why-im-still-reading-this">remind-me-why-im-still-reading-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=impossibly-slow-read">impossibly-slow-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=kinda-sorta-teared-up-a-bit">kinda-sorta-teared-up-a-bit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=fantasy-la-la-la">fantasy-la-la-la</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=ya-fantasy-romance">ya-fantasy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=eh-ish">eh-ish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10376232-saania-zee-jamal?shelf=massive-disappointment">massive-disappointment</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711054661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5384874317425386822"><i>PHEW.</i><br/>Why, if that wasn't the most laborious reading process of my life if ever I had one.<br/><br/>...okay, that's an exaggeration.<br/><s>(noitsnot)</s><br/><br/>
  <b>
    <i>“The whispers taunt me. 'Why? Why?'<br/><br/>It’s a question they ask over and over again. And my answer is always the same. <br/><br/>'Shut the fuckity fuck up.'<br/><br/>But no matter how many times I answer the whispers, they keep asking, because they don’t believe me.”</i>
  </b>
<br/><br/><s>(okyesitis)</s><br/><br/>Miiiight have tweaked the quote a little bit there, but that's how it bloody should've been. Sorry for </span>
  <span id="freeText5384874317425386822" style="display:none"><i>PHEW.</i><br>Why, if that wasn't the most laborious reading process of my life if ever I had one.<br><br>...okay, that's an exaggeration.<br><s>(noitsnot)</s><br><br>
  <b>
    <i>“The whispers taunt me. 'Why? Why?'<br><br>It’s a question they ask over and over again. And my answer is always the same. <br><br>'Shut the fuckity fuck up.'<br><br>But no matter how many times I answer the whispers, they keep asking, because they don’t believe me.”</i>
  </b>
<br><br><s>(okyesitis)</s><br><br>Miiiight have tweaked the quote a little bit there, but that's how it bloody should've been. Sorry for just spoiling literally 70% of the book, but this is for your own good. I shit you not, you cannot go five pages without Adelina and her damn whispers and illusions plaguing you once again AAARGUUGHHHHH.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486321462ra/21904041.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>How is it that a writer manages to give me the story I wanted and I'm still left bored and unsatisfied? Bad writing, that's what I tell you.<br><br>NOW BEFORE ANYONE DECIDES TO RUN AT ME WITH A BATTLESWORD, HEAR ME OUT. I gave her a shot, I really did. But after reading three books, I've realized that while she's got imagination on her side, Marie Lu is simply not a good writer. (Disclaimer: this is <b>
  <i><u>my personal opinion</u> and not the holy universal truth.</i>
</b>)<br><br>Her one redeeming quality lies in the fact that she can <b>create</b> a YA-perfect story... she just doesn't know how to <b>tell</b> one. In a way that doesn't hold the power to bore you to death at least.<br><br>Bland writing's been a constant throughout the entirety of the series, so you must be wondering, what made <i>The Rose Society</i> so special for me? (92.8% chance you're not actually wondering that but hey, now you know.) And the reason behind that is simple: that book made me FEEL. <br><br>No, it still didn't have much improvement to offer in the writing department, but at least there were characters to make up for it. Characters with complexities, with evolving relationships and most significantly—people worth caring about. I found myself forming a connection with sweet ol' Magiano, a brilliant new addition to the crew; with Violetta, who I gave about 0.1 shits about before; with Enzo and what could have been; with Rafaelle who just really, really needs a bear-hug; and heck, even with Teren of all folks, someone I'd loathed with a passion in the first book.<br><br>And then those very same characters took a nosedive right into flatland here. I honestly don't know why or where or what went wrong with this one, but <i>everything</i> just fell flat. Anything remotely exciting only pops up in the last fifty pages or so and by that point, I'd already stopped giving a damn about anyone. <i>Especially</i> Adelina. There are antiheroes you inexplicably seem to love and then there are antiheroes you just want to use as your personal punching bags.<br><br>I'll let you guess which category she falls into.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486321462ra/21904042.gif" width="380" height="290" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's like the longer I kept on reading, the more I ceased to care. Which is why it ended up taking three whole painstaking months to finally get this jig over with.<br><br>Despite all the shit that happens along the way, the fault lies not within the story, not at all. Truth be told, this is almost exactly the way I'd have ended it myself! But none of that matters when the execution isn't done right. You can use all the right ingredients and mix it as you like, but only a good chef knows how to spice it up and present a dish that makes you go W O W. And with what we get in <i>The Midnight Star</i>—let's just say Gordon Ramsay would not be amused. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486321462ra/21904043.gif" width="400" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Final rating: 1.5 stars</u><br>__________________________<br><br><b>Book songs: <i>Exhile</i> &amp; <i>Brother</i> by Eastghost</b><br>__________________________</span>
  <a data-text-id="5384874317425386822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15683898466400023457"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478525234ra/21081425.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm not going to lie and say this wasn't a sad book. I also felt like maybe there should have been a little bit more to it. I felt like it was - here you go, some evilness, some prophecies, some deaths, the end. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478525234ra/21081426.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>That being said, I'm sort of glad it didn't drag out like some books. Marie Lu got to the point of all things and brought it to where it was supposed to go. I really want to put a wonderful myth from the book in my review but that will give away too much.<br/><br/>I have loved Adelina through the </span>
  <span id="freeText15683898466400023457" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478525234ra/21081425.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm not going to lie and say this wasn't a sad book. I also felt like maybe there should have been a little bit more to it. I felt like it was - here you go, some evilness, some prophecies, some deaths, the end. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478525234ra/21081426.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That being said, I'm sort of glad it didn't drag out like some books. Marie Lu got to the point of all things and brought it to where it was supposed to go. I really want to put a wonderful myth from the book in my review but that will give away too much.<br><br>I have loved Adelina through the whole book. Yes, she did evil things, but look at all the evil things that were done to her and her kind. She just couldn't forget them. She also had kindness in her. We see in through out the books here and there and especially in this book. She did one of the most selfless acts of all time. <br><br>I have nothing else to say. I'm just sad. But that myth I was talking about, it's the only bright star for me. When you read the book you will know what I mean. <br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/11/the-midnight-star-by-marie-lu.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9702613659455926363">I've loved Adelina from the very beginning of this series. I love that she's ruthless and doesn't apologize for going after what she wants. Sure she's maybe a bit crazy and definitely mean, but I have rooted for her from the first page.<br/><br/>This portion of the journey is not what I was expecting. I love where Marie went with it and the choices she made.<br/><br/>Yes, I'm being intentionally vague.<br/>Yes, I had a serious case of the feels.<br/>Yes, it will be worth the wait. <br/><br/>**Huge thanks to G.P. Putnam's Sons Books fo</span>
  <span id="freeText9702613659455926363" style="display:none">I've loved Adelina from the very beginning of this series. I love that she's ruthless and doesn't apologize for going after what she wants. Sure she's maybe a bit crazy and definitely mean, but I have rooted for her from the first page.<br /><br />This portion of the journey is not what I was expecting. I love where Marie went with it and the choices she made.<br /><br />Yes, I'm being intentionally vague.<br />Yes, I had a serious case of the feels.<br />Yes, it will be worth the wait. <br /><br />**Huge thanks to G.P. Putnam's Sons Books for Young Readers and Edelweiss for providing the arc in exchange for an honest review**<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17563754921128813398">Might edit the rating later, because I am influenced by that wonderful ending -- which, to be honest, was the highlight of the entire book. I'm a bit conflicted, yet satisfied. I think I expected <i>more</i>, possibly from the whole series. My initial expectations and desires, to read a villain's tale, one filled with cunning and cleverness and ruthlessness, did somewhat materialize but combined with a dose of madness that partially stripped the beauty of the concept. I'm not gonna lie -- in terms of p</span>
  <span id="freeText17563754921128813398" style="display:none">Might edit the rating later, because I am influenced by that wonderful ending -- which, to be honest, was the highlight of the entire book. I'm a bit conflicted, yet satisfied. I think I expected <i>more</i>, possibly from the whole series. My initial expectations and desires, to read a villain's tale, one filled with cunning and cleverness and ruthlessness, did somewhat materialize but combined with a dose of madness that partially stripped the beauty of the concept. I'm not gonna lie -- in terms of plot, this finale was not grand. It seemed to drag and when the novel is quite short, you have a double problem. Sometimes I turned reading this into a chore, because I knew if I put it on indefinite hold, I'll never finish it. <br /><br />The end of The Young Elites journey is bittersweet. My heart broke yet again as certain characters followed their predictable destinies and I appreciated the lovely, heartwarming conjuring of new and past relationships, be it amorous or platonic. Originality and myth is etched into the last pages and I'm pleasantly surprised by the outcome. <br /><br />Good-bye, mi Adelinetta. Good-bye, Roses and Daggers. You were wonderful. </span>

<div id="review_1881322421" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1881322421" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1881322421?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fave-couple">fave-couple</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1881322421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8608797996301658083"><i>
  <blockquote>“Some say that, once upon a time, she had a prince, a father, a society of friends. Others say that she was once a wicked queen, a worker of illusions, a girl who brought darkness across the lands. Still others say that she once had a sister, and that she loved her dearly. Perhaps all of these are true.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>I absolutely adore this entire series</b> and for me, this was a fairly satisfying conclusion to the trilogy. I think Marie Lu is great at endings, she leaves them open-ended enough you can add t</span>
  <span id="freeText8608797996301658083" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“Some say that, once upon a time, she had a prince, a father, a society of friends. Others say that she was once a wicked queen, a worker of illusions, a girl who brought darkness across the lands. Still others say that she once had a sister, and that she loved her dearly. Perhaps all of these are true.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>I absolutely adore this entire series</b> and for me, this was a fairly satisfying conclusion to the trilogy. I think Marie Lu is great at endings, she leaves them open-ended enough you can add to the world in your head beyond the story, but closed enough you have closure and aren't wondering what happened to all the characters. So I definitely appreciated the ending of this series, it wrapped up most of the story and the characters well, but my main disappointment is that I felt some characters stories were left a little hanging and the storyline took a weird direction which I didn't feel was foreshadowed enough. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499234536ra/23207149.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499234536ra/23207148.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One of my first issues with this book was that the ending took a little turn towards a plot direction that seemed out of place to me. While the first two books focussed on the characters, and especially Adelina's quest for power, the third introduced a complication and fantasy element that wasn't explored much until this book. While it was foreshadowed a tiny bit at the end of The Rose Society, I still felt a little thrown off when this element came into play - and plot wise it did feel a little messy. It's easy to recover from, and it's not like it's so totally wild it ruined the story, but I did think it threw things off a little. <br><br>My other complaint was that I was a little dissatisfied with some of the charaters storylines - specifically Enzo's and Raffaele's and Mauve and Lucents. Raffaele and Enzo just deserved more closure and I wanted more about what happened to Raffaele after - and Mauve and Lucent weren't in it enough. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“You cannot harden your heart to the future just because of your past. You cannot use cruelty against yourself to justify cruelty to others.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br>But <b>beside all that</b> I really liked the conclusion to this trilogy. The characters remained as diabolical and twisted as they were earlier in the series - Adelina's arc came to a conclusion in a way I was really satisfied with, and I also really liked the addition of Magiano and his role in this book. <br><br>I've always praised this book for it's ambiguous characters and morally grey situations and that trend definitely continues throughout this series. Characters make decisions and change their behaviours and it's definitely open to discussion as to who deserved their ending, who didn't and who is truly good or evil. I love that about this series, and I love that Marie Lu didn't give us definitive answers. The beautify of this series is it's ambiguity and how open-ended it is. I'm so glad Marie Lu maintained that to the end. <br><br>The ending of this book is very controversial, but I personally was okay with it and it left me satisfied. This entire series I hold so close to my heart, and I wish less people dnf'ed it right at the start before it really gets good. <br><br>This series is full of flawed, complex characters who aren't all trying to make the right decision. It subverts so many tropes and presents us with characters who are motivated by greed, anger, hate, jealousy and fear, but also love and want and a sharp desire for justice. Truly, I think this is one of the most original series in ya, with characters who don't fit into the typical YA tropes but exist for their own benefit and act in a way that purely is to satisfy their own needs. On top of that it has amazing representation, worldbuiding and plot which never got boring for me.<br><br>I know I am literally the LAST person to read this series, but if you still haven't you definitely should. It's one of my favourite series now and I couldn't recommend it highly enough. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“You are a light,” she replies gently. “And when you shine, you shine bright.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8608797996301658083" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1869990731" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1869990731" />
    <a title="P " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25327841-p"><img alt="P " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489853536p2/25327841.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1869990731?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="P " class="user" itemprop="url" name="P " href="/user/show/25327841-p">P </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25327841-p?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1869990731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15872235959736078011"><b>
  <blockquote>“You are a light,” she replies gently. “And when you shine, you shine bright.” </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483944289i/21664237._SY540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm speechless. The ending is purely beautiful and inspirational. I loved Magiano, Adelina and Sergio, these characters are virile and push the story forward efficiently that I can't see how this book can be this good without them. Marie Lu managed to link the myth of Gods and Goddesses with the superpowers of the Elites very well, power always comes with a prize and it must be paid sooner or later. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480672475ra/21336702.gif' width='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483810353ra/21651708.gif' width='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479613716ra/21213568.gif' width='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483944523ra/21664258.gif' width='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was all t</span>
  <span id="freeText15872235959736078011" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“You are a light,” she replies gently. “And when you shine, you shine bright.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483944289i/21664237._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm speechless. The ending is purely beautiful and inspirational. I loved Magiano, Adelina and Sergio, these characters are virile and push the story forward efficiently that I can't see how this book can be this good without them. Marie Lu managed to link the myth of Gods and Goddesses with the superpowers of the Elites very well, power always comes with a prize and it must be paid sooner or later. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480672475ra/21336702.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483810353ra/21651708.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479613716ra/21213568.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483944523ra/21664258.gif" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was all the feels before I started reading The Midnight Stars. My heart was full of darkness. I wanted to see Adelina exact her revenge and claim what she wanted, but at some point, I felt it overwhelmed me, the darkness was so thick and crushed my lungs until it was hard to breath. There're many unnecessary fillers made me question the things that happened in this book without foreshadowing, too, and this is why The Midnight Star is my least favorite of all. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“There was once a time when darkness shrouded the world, and the darkness had a queen.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>One year passed since The Rose Society and Adelina built her kingdom on blood and cruelty. She gets what she wants, yet she always wants more. I had a hunch then that this was going to be her downfall, and I've never guessed wrong. Adelina is beyond redemption as Raffaele tells Violetta. Her heart is so rotten, and I didn't understand why Magiano was still beside her. Perhaps he loves her ? I think so. But there's something between their relationship making me speculate that Magiano is the only one who loves Adeliana, but on the other hand she fool herself heavily that she loves him. Despite the fact that she's just lonely and wants somone to hold on to, in my opinion, her love for Magiano is not real.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483944289ra/21664238.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As for Terren, his obsession for his queen is deep and struck me in my chest for what he's done for human racial purity. I get attached to his charcter more than the others, even Enzo, his dark side is palpable and captured my attention entirely. Magiano, I loved his playful side, and the way he soothes Adelina broke my heart. His development slowly proceeds, which showed me that I didn't ship the wrong guy. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“She walks to the boy, tilts her head up at him, and smiles. He bends down to kiss her. Then he helps her onto the horse, and she rides away with him to a faraway place, until they can no longer be seen.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Although Violetta is not my favorite character, she still steals the scene in this book. Her character is a conflict to her sister's wicked mind. While Adelina wants to find her sister among the war she wages, she still blames her for what happened in the last book. This confused me sometimes, yet I could understand why she was like this.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482954862ra/21566071.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Even now, decades later, I fear nothing so much as the open ocean at night, with darkness stretching around me in every direction.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>The actual rating of The Midnight Star isn't 4 stars after all, it's more like 3.85 stars for me if I compared this with The Young Elites. But I still enjoyed it. It's a perfect ending to this unputdownable series.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464316245ra/19226120.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://goo.gl/z93Sx2">https://goo.gl/z93Sx2</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15872235959736078011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
