<span id="freeTextContainer11927435245149914969"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517943384ra/25014909.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i> “Where will you go, when the clock strikes twelve? <br/>What will you do, when you face yourself? <br/>How will you live, knowing what you’ve done? <br/>How will you die, if your soul’s already gone?” </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/><i> “There was once a time when darkness shrouded the world, and the darkness had a queen.” </i> <br/>After her victory Adelina is now queen of Kenettra. But one city is not enough. Slowly she conquers other cities, other countries.<br/>Soon she rules with fear and darkness. <br/>As the war between the two groups go </span>
  <span id="freeText11927435245149914969" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517943384ra/25014909.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> “Where will you go, when the clock strikes twelve? <br>What will you do, when you face yourself? <br>How will you live, knowing what you’ve done? <br>How will you die, if your soul’s already gone?” </i> <br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br><i> “There was once a time when darkness shrouded the world, and the darkness had a queen.” </i> <br>After her victory Adelina is now queen of Kenettra. But one city is not enough. Slowly she conquers other cities, other countries.<br>Soon she rules with fear and darkness. <br>As the war between the two groups go on something dark settles around the world. <br>Taking something from the Underworld has its price and now the Young Elite sees the world pay its depth. <br>This book was so filled with action, love, revenge, betrayal and darkness. <br>We see enemies and allies, and we see them change their positions. <br>This was a perfect ending for the trilogy. ♥️<br>P.S. I even cried in the end. And I never cry. <br><br>Characters ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Adelina is still one of my favorite characters of all time. Marie Lu did a great work creating her. The voices in her head, the illusions, the darkness - all of them are slowly trying to take over control. Conquering all those countries, all these cities and bringing fear over the people, so they obey, take its toll. <br>The feeling of loneliness, the fear of betrayal is hunting her every step she takes. All of that made her such a realistic, dark and twisted character. Also the character development was just fascinating! <br>The other characters, new and old, are also created in a perfect, realistic way. I fell in love with a cute thief always looking out for Adelina. <br><br>World ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>The new cities, the new powers - all of that turns into dust when looking at the places that appear in this book. There’s something beyond the mortal world that mixes with it. <br>Something that only Elites can see. <br><br>Relationships ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br><i> “His lips touch my forehead, then my mouth. <br>And then, as if he understands me better than anyone in the world, he whispers, “It will make this night a little less dark.” </i> <br>I can only repeat it: “my love” will forever be my weakness. <br>And the guy saying it to Adelina is it to. <br>The way he always makes her smile, the way he cares for her and tries to make everything better for her. <br>He’s probably the most adorable, cute and wonderful guy in this world. ♥️ <br>Even though the relationship between Adelina and her sister is weakened it takes a different level in this book. <br>In the end they’re both the only family they have. <br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>I need to say: this book isn’t filled with as many quotes as the other two books, but it’s still rather filled with it. <br>The way Marie Lu writes is beautiful and addictive and now she is one of my favorite authors because of that trilogy. <br><i> “After a lifetime of darkness, I want to leave something behind that is made of light.” </i></span>

<div id="review_1591296805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1591296805" />
    <a title="Anja H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h"><img alt="Anja H." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559051853p2/6054186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1591296805?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anja H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anja H." href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h">Anja H.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1591296805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11701485018892283872"><b>*4.75 OTHERWORLDLY STARS*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"There was once a time when darkness shrouded the world, and the darkness had a queen.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Nope. Nope. Nooooope.<br/>This book has me sooooo damn <i>conflicted</i>, I don't even know where to start with this review or how to wrap my head around everything that's happened and that this trilogy just officially ended!<br/>I don't even know whether I freaking <b>love</b> or absolutely <b>loathe</b> that godforsaken ending, I'm just completely <b>in shock</b> right now.<br/><br/>This is still one of the <b>darkest</b> series I ha</span>
  <span id="freeText11701485018892283872" style="display:none"><b>*4.75 OTHERWORLDLY STARS*</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"There was once a time when darkness shrouded the world, and the darkness had a queen.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Nope. Nope. Nooooope.<br />This book has me sooooo damn <i>conflicted</i>, I don't even know where to start with this review or how to wrap my head around everything that's happened and that this trilogy just officially ended!<br />I don't even know whether I freaking <b>love</b> or absolutely <b>loathe</b> that godforsaken ending, I'm just completely <b>in shock</b> right now.<br /><br />This is still one of the <b>darkest</b> series I have ever read, hands down. Despite the fact that we saw <b>Adelina</b> change from an insecure girl who just wanted to be loved to a tyrannical, cruel woman, I never really hated or disliked her. That's a feat that not everyone can accomplish! Even though she became so dark and twisted, she was still likeable. I loved that in the end she slowly let go of her darkness again, and that ending was absolutely perfect yet heartbreaking for her at the same time!<br />Also, don't even get me started on <b>Magiano</b> because I could just rant on and on about how much I love him, but I'll spare you all from that and just say that he's an absolutely wonderful character that I fell in love with from the first moment he appeared. <i>Forget Enzo, I'm team Magiano!</i><br /><br />It was great to see all the major characters from all the previous books come together to surpass the big final hurdle that was this book. They had to put their differences aside, whether they were rivals, enemies or friends. I feel like lots of <i>lessons</i> could be learned from these books and The Young Elites will forever go down as one of my favorite book trilogies in history.<br /><br />The one thing I can say for certain right now is that Marie Lu is one hell of a brilliant writer and I'm reading whatever she publishes next!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11701485018892283872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1403986761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1403986761" />
    <a title="Cindy ✩☽♔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3222333-cindy"><img alt="Cindy ✩☽♔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605643833p2/3222333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1403986761?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy ✩☽♔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy ✩☽♔" href="/user/show/3222333-cindy">Cindy ✩☽♔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=otps-feels">otps-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222333-cindy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1403986761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8365203504948352309"><b> "We were never meant to exist, Adelina," he says. "And we will never exist again. But we cannot take the entire world with us." He meets my gaze. "No matter how it has wronged us." </b> <br/><br/>As has been said, we are a part of the books we read, and the books we read become a part of us. <br/><br/>Well if that is true, I can honestly say, a part of me is missing. This book stole a part of me and I don't think I will ever get it back. And you know what? That's okay. It is sad, painful, undoubtedly beautiful and ter</span>
  <span id="freeText8365203504948352309" style="display:none"><b> "We were never meant to exist, Adelina," he says. "And we will never exist again. But we cannot take the entire world with us." He meets my gaze. "No matter how it has wronged us." </b> <br><br>As has been said, we are a part of the books we read, and the books we read become a part of us. <br><br>Well if that is true, I can honestly say, a part of me is missing. This book stole a part of me and I don't think I will ever get it back. And you know what? That's okay. It is sad, painful, undoubtedly beautiful and terribly bittersweet; but somehow that's okay. <br><br>This book proves to me once again that Marie Lu must enjoy making me suffer. Secretly, she is somewhere hiding away feeding off my suffering. While this book was rather short in comparison to the others, I think it kept the story tight and moving continuously. Though to be perfectly honest I certainly would not have minded a few more chapters. Because I love these characters and this story so much. <br><br>As we've come to expect from Marie Lu she takes all the wonderfully complex characters, conflicts and themes we've come to love and really drives them home. This book is nothing short of amazing. <br><br><u> Adelina and Magiano </u><br>These two are everything!<br><a href="http://s1326.photobucket.com/user/cincin1993/media/giphy-1_zpsckia17cy.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476307665ra/20825784.gif" alt=" photo giphy-1_zpsckia17cy.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i> “No one is forcing you to stay here, of course, in service to me. You are free to come and go as you wish. You’re a Elite, after all. The greatest of mankind.” <br><br>Magino frowns. “No,” he agrees. “No one is forcing me to stay.” <br>---<br>“Do you still remember the fire? Under the stars?” he asks, suddenly shy, and I feel innocent for the first time in a long while. <br><br>“I remember what we were doing,” I reply with a small smile. <br><br>A laugh escapes his lips. Then his expression turns serious. “You asked me whether or not I miss my old life,” he whispers, his voice now hoarse. “Do you know what I miss the most? That night.” <br><br>My heart skips a beat, aching in sudden sadness. “And what about the girl you once sat beside, on that night? Do you miss her too?”<br><br>“She is still here,” he answers. “That is why I stay.” <br>---<br>“You are so full of light,” I say after a moment. “You align with joy, and I with fear and fury. If you could see into my thoughts, you would surely turn away. So why would you stay with me, even if we return to Kenettra and resume our lives?”<br><br>“You paint me as a saint,” he murmurs. “But I aligned with greed solely to prevent that.” <br><br>Even now, he can make my lips twitch with a smile. “I’m serious, Magiano.”<br><br>“As am I. None of us are saints. I have seen your darkness, yes, and know your struggle. I won’t deny it.” He touches my chin with one hand. At this gesture, the whispers seem to settle, pushed away where I can’t hear them. “But you are also passionate and ambitious and loyal. You are a thousand things, mi Adelinetta, not just one. Do not reduce yourself to that.” </i><br><br>As I have said before, Magiano is Adelina’s light. He sees her, all of her, and he is unafraid. He quiets the dark whispers in her mind. He keeps the nightmares at bay. But most importantly, he loves her. Until the very end he loves her, even in death. <br><a href="http://s1326.photobucket.com/user/cincin1993/media/15476172_zpsthyiluau.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476307468ra/20825774.gif" alt=" photo 15476172_zpsthyiluau.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ “I’m going to follow her, of course,” Magiano says. “As the night sky turns. When she appears on the other side of the world, I will be there, and when she returns here, so will I.” <a href="http://s1326.photobucket.com/user/cincin1993/media/16955936_zpsq7chy6pl.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475168467ra/20691410.gif" alt=" photo 16955936_zpsq7chy6pl.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><u> Enzo and Adelina </u><br>I do not doubt that these two loved each other once. But their love was not built to last. This book proves that. Both Enzo and Adelina have darkness, ambition, and fire in their hearts. Neither of them needed more of it. While they may have loved each other, they did not need each other. <br><br>And that is reflected quite well in this book, just as Magiano became Adelina’s light, Enzo had found his light long ago. <br><br><i> Raffaele wonders whom Enzo is thinking about. It is not Adelina, but a girl long gone, from a happier time in his past. <br>---<br>He turns his head weakly in the direction of the ocean. The black pools in his eyes finally vanish, and a name drifts from his lips. He says it so quietly I nearly miss it. It is not my name, but the name of another girl, one he had known and loved long ago. </i> <br><br>Enzo may have been Adelina's first love, but clearly, he was not the love of her life and she was surely not his. <br><br><u> Teren and Adelina </u> <br>I can't say these two had anything close to a good relationship. But I suppose I can say they had a sort of understanding. Two people who could see the monster inside the other. Two people who were in constant battle with inner demons. In another life, perhaps, they could have been friends. <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <i> Teren is dead, and I do not know why I cry for him. <br>I have killed and destroyed too. I have hurt. Perhaps we have always been one and the same, just as he used to tell me. And now that he's gone, I feel a sudden rush of exhaustion, a freeing grief. His death marks the end of a long chapter in my life. </i>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><u> Raffaele and Adelina </u><br>I missed these two. They were so sweet for most of the first book, and then got completely wrecked by the end of the first book and much of second. However, we finally see some hope for these two in this book. Because Raffaele finally recognizes, that despite his best intentions, he hurt Adelina more than he could have imagined. When he turned his back on her he never imagined that that meant saying goodbye to the girl he once knew. Perhaps, if he had helped, embraced her instead of sending her away things would have been different. And a life of what ifs is the most painful kind. <br><br><i> It is my fault, what Adelina has become. My fault that it is too late. </i><br>---<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <i> The first time Raffaele ever saw Adelina, it was a stormy-wracked night that changed her life and, indeed, the world. He recalls looking down from the window in his Dalia lodging to see a girl with silver-bright hair, conjuring an illusion of darkness such that he had never seen. He remembers the day she first came to his chambers in Estenzia, when Enzo was still alive and she was still innocent, and the way she looked up at him with her uncertain, damaged gaze. He remembers her test, and what he said to Enzo that night. How long ago that had been. How he had judged her wrongly. <br><br>Raffaele looks around the clearing, searching for one last figure. He looks high and low hoping for footprints in the snow or shadows in the forest line. He wishes he could still sense the energy of the living, could pinpoint where she is. But even then, he knows that he would arrive at the same answer as the others. <br><br>Adelina is gone. </i>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>But in the end, I think they finally understood each other, finally forgave each other. <br><br><u> Adelina and Violetta </u><br>It's the third and final book, yet I am still not sure how I feel about these two. Actually, that's not true. I know how I feel about them, I just feel like I may be in the minority.<br><br>I understand the familial love, truly I do. But still, I cannot bring myself to fully like Violetta. And I think that stems primarily from the fact that I love Adelina so much. She's made a lot of mistakes, a lot, but she led a very hard life. She suffered more than anyone should ever have to, and no matter how many times Adelina or anyone else reminds me how much Violetta loved her, I will say this, Violetta never did anything to help protect Adelina from their father. Violetta may be goodness and she may be light, but I think that is greatly due to the fact that for most of her life all she has ever received is love. Love from her father, love from her sister, from all her suitors and nearly everyone she meets. And while I appreciate her goodness, she lacks the one thing I look for above all else, strength. The strength to stand up for something, the willingness to going against the accepted norm. The will to fight for what she believes and knows is right. It constantly felt like Adelina was the only one fighting, and Violetta was just along for the ride. <br><br>And in the end, once again, it was Adelina who made the greatest sacrifice. When I got to the end I was left thinking, what did Violetta do that she earned this end? What has she sacrificed? Adelina, Enzo, Raffaele and even Teren, they all suffered so much. They'd lived though so much and they all certainly deserved better than they got. I suppose, however, that at least in the end Violetta finally did something I appreciated. She finally fought for her sister in her own way. Though I will always feel Violetta never fought for Adelina as much as Adelina fought for her, and that is my problem. Nevertheless, I loved Adelina until the very end and, like Magiano, I respected her decision. <br><br>It is important to note that it takes a great book to make me appreciate and fully reflect on its characters and storyline. This book does just that. <br><br>Despite my lingering heartache, I can say this book is an absolute gem. I loved every second of it and would be more than willing ride along for this journey again. As I've said, the ending is very bittersweet. But I truly appreciated how Marie Lu concluded this magnificent journey. The ending made sense, it was in character and this was the kind of story and end that legends are made of.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8365203504948352309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1398070351" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1398070351" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1398070351?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1398070351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4498380825744257669">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/10/review-midnight-star-by-marie-lu.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>The Midnight Star by Marie Lu<br/>Book Three of The Young Elites series<br/>Publisher: G.P. Putnam's Sons Books for Young Readers<br/>Publication Date: October 11, 2016<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>There was once a time when darkness shrouded the world, and the darkness had a queen.<br/><br/>Adelina Amouteru is done suffering. She’s turned her back on those who have betrayed her and achieved the ultimate revenge: victory.</span>
  <span id="freeText4498380825744257669" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br><br>***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/10/review-midnight-star-by-marie-lu.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br><br>The Midnight Star by Marie Lu<br>Book Three of The Young Elites series<br>Publisher: G.P. Putnam's Sons Books for Young Readers<br>Publication Date: October 11, 2016<br>Rating: 4 stars<br>Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br><br>Summary (from Goodreads):<br><br>There was once a time when darkness shrouded the world, and the darkness had a queen.<br><br>Adelina Amouteru is done suffering. She’s turned her back on those who have betrayed her and achieved the ultimate revenge: victory. Her reign as the White Wolf has been a triumphant one, but with each conquest her cruelty only grows. The darkness within her has begun to spiral out of control, threatening to destroy all that she’s achieved.<br><br>Adelina’s forced to revisit old wounds when a new danger appears, putting not only Adelina at risk, but every Elite and the very world they live in. In order to save herself and preserve her empire, Adelina and her Roses must join the Daggers on a perilous quest—though this uneasy alliance may prove to be the real danger.<br><br>Bestselling author Marie Lu concludes Adelina's story with this haunting and hypnotizing final installment to the Young Elites series. <br><br>What I Liked:<br><br>***SPOILER-FREE REVIEW. There may be spoilers if you haven't read The Young Elites or The Rose Society, but you're safe in terms of The Midnight Star.***<br><br>The Midnight Star is an intense, dark, and thrilling conclusion to a fascinating and utterly unique fantasy series. I am blown away by Marie Lu's storytelling, her writing, and her stories in general. I don't typically read books so dark (at least in Young Adult), but I couldn't resist this series. And I'm glad I didn't - it was a magnificent and heartbreaking trilogy.<br><br>This final novel starts about a year or so after the end of The Rose Society (so it's been about two years since the beginning of The Young Elites). Adelina is suffering from the voices and hallucinations and nightmares, even more so than usual. But she's also very successful in her conquests - she is now the Queen of the Sealands, and she wants more. But every newly conquered territory fails to have what Adelina is looking for - her sister, who fled. And every new territory brings more and more assassination attempts, and more cruelty from Adelina. But there is a growing danger that is bigger than conquering lands and finding Violetta, and Adelina will find herself in the middle of the problem. To stop this growing chaos, she must learn to trust the Daggers that she has grown to hate. Sacrifices must be made, lives must be lost, and darkness will threaten to consume Adelina and the world, once and for all. <br><br>Upon finishing this book, I was speechless. My heart hurt, but it was also full to bursting. This book is not a happy and fluffy novel. There is only one way that this book could end (with variations), and it could not involve a cookie-cutter perfect HEA. I love how Lu put everything together, how she led readers to the ending, how everything fell apart and then bonded again.<br><br>Adelina gets more and more... villainous, shall we say? She's an antihero, a villain in this series. She's a cruel queen; she makes the laws very lenient for the marked, but harsh to the point of death for the unmarked. For all the times that she was hurt by the unmarked, she wants them to suffer by the hands of the marked. Adelina has become a ruthless tyrant, and everything fears her, hates her, and/or wants to kill her. Those who serve her, can they be trusted?<br><br>And yet, even though Adelina is quite the villain, we can clearly see just how human she once was, and still is. In her heart, she is doing what she thinks is right, but she is not naive or misguided. She wants to do right by the marked, which means punishing the unmarked (in her mind). We see her struggling with her hallucinations, with her unstable powers, with her feelings for Magiano and her grip on humanity. Honestly, as tyrannical and cruel as Adelina was in this book, she was also extremely human. My heart broke for her over and over. She deteriorates slowly but surely, in terms of her power (and her mind, a little), and it's sad to see how she lets her Elite power and her political power get to her. <br><br>This book is told in Adelina's first-person POV, as well as Raffaele's third-person POV. There are one or two chapters that are written in another character's third-person POV, but Adelina's first-person and Raffaele's third-person POV are the most important and most prevalent ones. I loved reading from Adelina's POV, but I also liked seeing another perspective. This mode of storytelling isn't my favorite (dual POV is fine but switching from first- to third-person is a little weird), but I think it works well in this trilogy.<br><br>The cast of secondary characters is relatively the same as in the previous books, with a few new ones here and there. I loved Magiano - he is probably my favorite character in the book. I need to reread The Young Elites and see how he came about in the series (I remember him from The Rose Society but not The Young Elites). Violetta is important in this book, but not present all the time. I didn't love her or hate her. Magiano and Sergio, are two of the best characters in this book. <br><br>I love Lu's writing, and the world-building of this book. Lu has a quality of writing that isn't quite lyrical, but it flows so well and has a rhythm to it. And her craftsmanship is so perfect - the world-building, the characters, the setting, the plot. Seriously, I'm having trouble finding flaws (not that I'm looking for them, specifically!). <br><br>There is romance in this book, and it's probably the strongest and most shippiest in this book than the other two. If you've read The Young Elites and The Rose Society, then you know the pair... Adelina and Magiano. There are some really sweet scenes in this book, which you wouldn't expect because Adelina is so ruthless. Magiano loves her, and while Adelina is purposeful in her cruelty, she loves him too. <br><br>I won't say a word about the ending, or even the plot and major events leading up to the climax... just know that you will be interested and hanging on to the edge of your seat and wanting to know how things will end. The ending crept up on me and I knew it was going to happen. But I liked how it happened. Lu knows how to deliver a powerful ending that is equal parts dark and light. <br><br>What I Did Not Like:<br><br>This isn't something negative about the book, but more of a suggestion - I highly recommend doing a reread of The Young Elites and The Rose Society (or at least The Rose Society) before reading this one. Lu does a good job of getting us back into the story (with recall and whatnot), but it would be immensely helpful to reread the books!<br><br>Would I Recommend It:<br><br>I highly recommend this book, and series in general. It is a very dark series (seriously though. Adelina is all kinds of cruel and cold), so if you're not into antiheroes and such, then maybe don't go for this one. And if you need a perfect HEA, then maybe avoid the series. The ending is good though, and it's exactly what the series needed. In any case, this is a really well-written fantasy series, and one that I'll be thinking about for a long time. <br><br>Rating:<br><br>4.5 stars. I'm rounding down to 4 stars (I have to, given certain things that I liked but didn't like but can't say here because spoilers), but I really enjoyed this book. I think it's my favorite of the series? It's hard to say. All of the books were so good!<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><strong>April 2016 EDIT</strong>: <a href="http://mashable.com/2016/04/21/the-midnight-star-cover-reveal-marie-lu/" rel="nofollow noopener">COVER</a>!!!!!!!<br><br><br><br><br><br>I. Need. It. Dyyyyiiiiinnnngggg from <i>The Rose Society.</i><br><br>Did you see my review of <i>
  <a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2015/09/review-rose-society-by-marie-lu.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose Society</a>
</i>? GO SEE WHY I AM DYING. <br><br><br>GIMMEEEEEEEE BOOK THREEEEEE.<br><br><strong>EDIT (January 19th, 2016): WE HAVE A TITLE!!!! <i>The Midnight Star</i>!!!!</strong><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436053035ra/15413003.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426542459ra/14043477.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413361234ra/11501383.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1417622805?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/36179502-rose">Rose</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1417622805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17919373366174730202">"We can all do better."<br/><i>We can all do better. </i><br/><br/>So, here I am, feeling <b>emo as fuck</b> after that ending. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476723311ra/20873941.gif' width='auto' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Things I expected from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28588345.The_Midnight_Star__The_Young_Elites___3_' title='The Midnight Star (The Young Elites, #3) by Marie Lu' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Midnight Star</a>:</b><br/><br/><b>• </b>some sort of a happy, or at least, meaningful ending<br/><b>• </b>lots of epicness and crazy battles<br/><b>• </b>something different that wasn't in the other books<br/><br/><b>What I got:</b><br/><br/>Well, I <i>definitely</i> got something new/different from this book.... <b>a boring first half</b>. There's a lot of words I could use to describe this series, and I never thought boring would be one of them. I literally</span>
  <span id="freeText17919373366174730202" style="display:none">"We can all do better."<br><i>We can all do better. </i><br><br>So, here I am, feeling <b>emo as fuck</b> after that ending. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476723311ra/20873941.gif" width="auto" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Things I expected from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28588345.The_Midnight_Star__The_Young_Elites___3_" title="The Midnight Star (The Young Elites, #3) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Star</a>:</b><br><br><b>• </b>some sort of a happy, or at least, meaningful ending<br><b>• </b>lots of epicness and crazy battles<br><b>• </b>something different that wasn't in the other books<br><br><b>What I got:</b><br><br>Well, I <i>definitely</i> got something new/different from this book.... <b>a boring first half</b>. There's a lot of words I could use to describe this series, and I never thought boring would be one of them. I literally felt like nothing happened in the first 50%- nothing of importance anyway. <br><br>Lots of battles or epicness? <i>Not reaaally</i>. I mean very few people can fight Adelina, and even less want to. And there was like two scenes where I thought things would get crazy, but still.. <b>the scenes were short and boring. </b><br><br>The ending...<b> no spoilers here</b>, but it left me partially regretting starting the series. I didn't feel anything for a good 90% of the book and then suddenly.. <i>PAIN</i>. Nothing that I wanted to happen actually happened, and I'm cool with that, but either way <b>everything felt meaningless</b>. I'm literally not elaborating on this at all because I don't want to ruin anything for anyone, so if you wanna know what happens: <u>continue reading</u>. <br><br><b>SPOILER ZONE, BEWARE: </b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[me when Enzo died:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415849462ra/11855406.gif" width="auto" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>me when Violetta died:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415849462ra/11855406.gif" width="auto" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>me when Teren died:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476723586ra/20873980.gif" width="auto" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>me when Adelina sacrifices herself for Violetta:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422397478ra/13498246.gif" width="auto" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So basically the only two interesting and complex characters died, and Violetta gets to live. I really couldn't care less about her, so I was kinda pissed that Adelina did that, but at the same time I know I would do the same for my sister so I can't hate. <br><br>It is a little disappointing because I feel like so many authors go in this direction, and it's so meaningless. <br><br>In the end everyone just goes back to how they were before the fever, <b>the Young Elites are erased</b>, Magiano lives on while the love of his life is gone, and <i>Violetta becomes queen</i>. And all this happens in like the last two chapters, while the rest of the story is about Adelina conquering lands for no reason at all. So what was the point of everything then?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

In order to save herself and preserve her empire, Adelina and her Roses must join the Daggers on a perilous quest—though this uneasy alliance may prove to be the real danger.</i>

I bet they're plaining to kill Adelina once they're done with the mission. I bet Raffaele is trying to control Enzo but he struggles. I bet Magiano will die, <i>I hope he doesn't because I like him so much,</i> but the thing is, they all are going to die. <br><br>I mean, how can any of them stay alive to rule? If he's alive, will he pick a side?<br><br>I have all these theories making me nuts so here's what I wrote at the end of my review for The Rose Society:<br><br><b>

Enzo will go insane. Probably kills Raffaele. </blockquote>

<div id="review_2088095289" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2088095289" />
    <a title="Nasom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom"><img alt="Nasom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520213174p2/67824881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2088095289?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasom" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom">Nasom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67824881-nasom?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2088095289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13203398311955772288">Hmm I don't know how I feel about this book. My real rating is between 3.5 to 4. I did like the plot and the unification of previous enemies for the good of the world but I wasn't satisfied with the characters.<br/><br/>There were a lot of supporting characters that were more prominent in previous books but were pushed aside in this. Majority of the book involves Adelina struggling with the whispers in her head. I felt like they focused too much on that. Like we get it! She hears things. It became repetit</span>
  <span id="freeText13203398311955772288" style="display:none">Hmm I don't know how I feel about this book. My real rating is between 3.5 to 4. I did like the plot and the unification of previous enemies for the good of the world but I wasn't satisfied with the characters.<br /><br />There were a lot of supporting characters that were more prominent in previous books but were pushed aside in this. Majority of the book involves Adelina struggling with the whispers in her head. I felt like they focused too much on that. Like we get it! She hears things. It became repetitive. <br /><br />We did get a glimpse of Teren's (love of my life) past which I liked because I always wanted to know what caused him to be the way he was.<br /><br />Also, I wanted more romance especially for Raffaele giving his past. I didn't care for Adelina's romance because she was honestly a terrible person (which I guess she was meant to be) and I did not understand why someone as joyous as her love interest would be in love with her. <br /><br />It ends in a bittersweet way. I knew it wasn't going to end in a happily ever after giving the history of the series so it was expected.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13203398311955772288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1961570380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1961570380" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1961570380?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=over-my-dead-body">over-my-dead-body</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=mary-sue-warning">mary-sue-warning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=unrealistic-main-characters">unrealistic-main-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=no-hell-no">no-hell-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=only-when-it-is-for-free">only-when-it-is-for-free</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=nothing-special">nothing-special</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=supernatural-stuff">supernatural-stuff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1961570380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15300032125797343217">1.5 stars. I never meant to give this series such low rating, the writing alone is far more decent than many other YA books out there to say the least. But damn! There is no lying to myself. Due to the following points, <i>The Midnight Star</i> is not a good YA fantasy novel:<br/><br/><b>(1) The political contexts in the story have gone from poorly construed to down right ridiculous:</b><br/><br/>If anyone told you <i>The Young Elites</i> series shares anything remotely similar with A Game of Thrones or Mistborn, they are freaking lyin</span>
  <span id="freeText15300032125797343217" style="display:none">1.5 stars. I never meant to give this series such low rating, the writing alone is far more decent than many other YA books out there to say the least. But damn! There is no lying to myself. Due to the following points, <i>The Midnight Star</i> is not a good YA fantasy novel:<br><br><b>(1) The political contexts in the story have gone from poorly construed to down right ridiculous:</b><br><br>If anyone told you <i>The Young Elites</i> series shares anything remotely similar with A Game of Thrones or Mistborn, they are freaking lying.<br><br>For example, two newly ascended young rulers, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Adelina and Maeve <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> are free to leave their kingdoms behind FOR MONTHS and no one has ever tried to overthrow them!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409721462ra/11013223.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>(2) It really is something when the author admits at the Acknowledgement that the Main Character, Adelina, is actually herself:</b><br><br>I. Have. No. Freaking. Word!<br><br>...and being an Angst Sue isn't even the worst of Adelina's problems, I promise you.<br><br>I can't stress this point enough: Adelina is not a realistic villain, nor is she a capable ruler, she isn't even smart enough to rule anything, not for long anyway. How she had managed to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ become queen and hold onto her power <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is completely beyond me. She is selfish, she is angry with her life, she is angry with everyone and with the Daggers' so-called 'betrayal', she wants to take her pain and bitterness out on everyone; all of the above only make her a butthurt <b>loser</b>, not a villain.<br> <br>To say the least, I hate losers like her.<br><br><b>(3) The lack of conflicts:</b> <br><br>Where the hell is the conflict? I had expected the Elites to fight among themselves but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[this never happens <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Everyone just be friendly with each other and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[goes on a quest to save the world <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, no hard feeling whatsoever. There isn't even a final showdown.<br><br><b>(4) The wasteful and meaningless characters' death:</b><br> <br>I have expected important characters to die, but I hate how those characters' deaths are delivered: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Enzo died in the most uneventful way (I feel that Ms. Lu just didn't want Enzo in the story anymore so she just killed him off without much planning), Teren got killed by some random monsters and he didn't even try to take Adelina and a few other Elites down with him before he died?<br><br>Don't even get me started with how Adelina suddenly becomes a saint and sacrifices her life in exchange for her sister Violetta's! This part is just freaking awful! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>(5) The romance/the hints of romance:</b><br><br>For the love of Hell, would Ms. Lu just please stop trying to pair her characters up and write romantic interaction among them!? Her 'romance scenes' are always as emotional and touching as a piece of rock.<br><br>LGTB couples (mainly Maeve/Lucent and Raffaele/Enzo) are thrown into the story to show OMG this series is SO INCLUSIVE! But in this book, NOTHING has been done about these couples! So, what is the point anyway?<br><br>On the side note, I am not convicted by the sisterly love between Adelina and Violetta neither. Adelina is an awful sister anyway and Violetta is so filled with goodness that she is no better than a Mary Sue.<br><br><b>(6) The story feels rushed:</b><br><br>A lot of details and background information have simply been ignored or glossed over throughout the story, the mythology jumps in and out of the story at random, I have a feeling that Ms. Lu had simply become bored and uninterested with her story when she penned this final book.<br><br><b>(7) The ending:</b> <br><br>I mean, how unrealistic and ridiculous can this ending get!? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[as a queen Adelina had treated at least half of her subjects like craps but in the end those same people simply accept Adelina's sister (who is now without any superhuman power) as their new queen? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493212961i/22592354.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vampirekiki.deviantart.com/art/Mana-354705039">http://vampirekiki.deviantart.com/art...</a>)<br><br>Plus <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130709618?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Natalie's review</i>
</a> reminds me the epilogue of this book hints that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Adelina isn't dead for real, she somehow manages to become a midnight star and meets Magiano again <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>! What kind of half-hearted bullshit ending is that!? <br><br><b>The Final Words:</b> Marie Lu claims in the Acknowledgement part this series is <i>the hardest thing she has ever written</i>, <b>my reaction to it is still to LOL.</b> I am sorry, Ms. Lu, you can't fool me. I can barely see enough effort in this story of yours to justify your claim.<br><br>Six YA books came and went, I'd thought: maybe, just maybe, Marie Lu would have matured as an author, but judging from how <i>The Midnight Star</i> has turned out, it's silly for me to think she would improve.<br><br>Review for <i>The Young Elites</i>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1164003124?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br>Review for <i>The Rose Society</i>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1546659056?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br><br><b>Extra:</b> well written YA fantasy novel with remotely believable world building and court's politic: Mistwood and its sequel (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/635250227?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a>)</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15300032125797343217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

	<tr>
		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aP9k+9M5Y1hIuOK00+7mr4JEm9nPvnYfJGmnOxQ2hExS2Q0paGeqMO+TVtUkG+xwVBt8EQEz+Hh/F+GK2XV21g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7foteQieCzzjs1OMsf+oTy56sCcnxY1sZQjZTp/sCC7X3ESrs8DCVESY5+1GCqKQ+CVX7+lIAws+dp//Uq/6tA==')})
  }
//]]>

Adelina’s black hair turned silver, her lashes went pale, and now she has only a jagged scar where her left eye once was. Her cruel father believes she is a malfetto, an abomination, ruining their family’s good name and standing in the way of their fortune. But some of the fever’s survivors are rumored to possess more than just scars—they are believed to have mysterious and powerful gifts, and though their identities remain secret, they have come to be called the Young Elites.\n\nTeren Santoro works for the king. As Leader of the Inquisition Axis, it is his job to seek out the Young Elites, to destroy them before they destroy the nation. He believes the Young Elites to be dangerous and vengeful, but it’s Teren who may possess the darkest secret of all. \n\nEnzo Valenciano is a member of the Dagger Society. This secret sect of Young Elites seeks out others like them before the Inquisition Axis can. But when the Daggers find Adelina, they discover someone with powers like they’ve never seen. \n\nAdelina wants to believe Enzo is on her side, and that Teren is the true enemy. But the lives of these three will collide in unexpected ways, as each fights a very different and personal battle. But of one thing they are all certain: Adelina has abilities that shouldn’t belong in this world. A vengeful blackness in her heart.
